</dataset><record>
<GmapID>0x80c2dadd1b9e6477:0xafbfa665d74bea92</GmapID><date>1441869068306< /date><pics>None</pics><user_id>111786517743281339317</user_id>< rating>

< review>
Another tea house within a few blocks of A Plus, Neighbors, and Tbay? Yep, and T4U has found a way to stand out from the other tea places with their Chamango drink. I didn't try it, but it seems to be a pretty stand out drink that isn't served at most other tea houses.

T4U is located in a small plaza on San Gabriel. There's a private parking lot for the plaza, but there's also street parking as well. It's a really tiny tea house, with only two or three tables and a couch area. I think there was another table outside with chairs around it, but when I came with my friend, every seat was taken and we had to resort to going elsewhere to drink our drinks.

There were a few drinks I wanted to try from T4U's top ten drinks, but I convinced myself to just get one. I tried the Sea Salt Cream Green Tea, which I have high expectations for. I thought it tasted fairly good. With the check-in offer, I received a large sized drink - and with the addition of boba, everything was still under $4. Boba was really good. Chewy and firm, with enough sweetness to give it flavor. It didn't detract from the green tea flavor either. Whenever I order this particular drink, I like to make sure that the cream is separate from the tea. I felt like the color of the tea was pretty similar to the cream, which made me think that maybe milk was added. But the tea was pretty good - not as "pure" as I have had from other places, but I liked it. I would probably put T4U's sea salt cream green tea in my top five, with this being the fifth compared to other tea houses.

My friend tried the honey green tea and the Hokkaido milk tea and thought they both were good.

Can't really comment much since I only tried one drink and I thought it was good. Service was fast and efficient - drinks came out in under 5 minutes. I wanted to try their Cassava cakes, but they were all out. I will be back to try their popular Chamango drink as well as their Cassava cake and popcorn chicken!

Credit card accepted on orders of more than $10, otherwise you can pay $0.40 to use the card. Don't forget to get a stamp card! If you can find a place to sit, they have Wi-Fi and board games for customers.<//review>

<time>1536805184575<//time><rating>5< /rating>< Text>
We're from out of town. Had to go to the Dollar Tree and we were starving. Pizza di Marco was in the same shopping center. We went there reluctantly...its definitely not a fancy place. But when the food came, it was great! And there was so much of it that we took half back to our hotel and ate it 2 nights later. It was still wonderful. We had the eggplant parmesan and garlic shrimp linguine. The dinner salad was huge as well, and very good. And there was plenty of fresh, toasted garlic bread. We will definitely go there or order from there whenever we come back to the Santa Clarita area. (They don't serve alcohol, so we enjoyed the leftovers with some wine in our hotel room.) Can't wait to try some of the other choices on the menu. Highly recommend this restaurant.<//Text>

< text>
Had high hopes, but this was a bummer of an experience. Such a bummer, in fact, that I felt compelled to write a review. Our service was beyond spotty - our server would disappear for long stretches of time, and we constantly had to ask busboys for her to come over. The appetizer plate resembled something I could put together at home. My dirty martini was just muddled pimento olives at the bottom of the shaker. The salad was okay, but my steak had no seasoning or flavor, and neither did the creamed spinach (a complaint repeated by my dining companions as well). One of my dining companions was given another table's order. We also had to request steak knives and non-salad forks. For the cost of the meal, it was incredibly disappointing. SF could use a great old steakhouse, but I'm afraid this isn't it. A chain restaurant like Ruth's Chris or Morton's would produce a more satisfying meal, for sure.< /text>

<Rating>2<//Rating><review>A shadow of its former glory.  I've been frequenting Alfred's for over a decade.  The excellence of their Manhattan's and Old Fashion's was diminished a year ago.  Then the management changed hands, the entire staff (which had worked there for decades) left.  Recently it was re-opened following a fire.  The decor is largely unchanged (bathrooms were overhauled without the classic martini wallpaper).  But the service is terrible, the meat isn't nearly as good as it was and not worth its price, several menu favorites are gone.  Alfred's is dead to me.  If you've never been, you'll find this to be a place that is certainly "above average", but long time patrons will notice that the magnificent "old world" spark that Alfred's maintained is now, officially, burned out.<//review>< pictures>

<rating>5</rating>< text>
Sexy, classy, historic-yet-modern. Love the dramatic & glamorous ambience: romantic lighting, rich red walls, tinted mirrors, chandeliers, flowers. Service was top-notch, from the hostess, to our waiter, and wait staff. Very knowledgeable sommelier with great reccomendations! Everyone was attentive & approachable. My hubby took me out for a date here last night. They have a great martini menu and other classic drinks with a modern twist. Started with the Vesper Martini which has a nice lemon flavor. We ordered Oysters Rockefeller and shared the Porterhouse Dinner for Two with a bottle of Syrah. This was more than enough food for two, and so delicious! The dinner comes with bananas foster for dessert, prepared at your table! Definitely a great place to have an intimate, special date night. Some tips: Do park at the Hilton hotel next door. It's valet, but covered by the restaraunt- just bring good tip money. Do dress cocktail/business casual/professional. Don't rush through this great, intimate, dinner experience.</text>

<text>Alfred's is my treat to myself. I've been exploring steakhouses in San Francisco for 15 years with a wide range of quality, service, and price. < Review>
So I went to this car wash 7/8/2020 around 6:30 pm. First of all, the dude that was directing me to get my wheel on the moving belt wasn't even paying attention to how he was directing my car. He was looking at something behind my car and just motioning for me to come forward, resulting in me hitting my wheel on the track. Anyway, I got in the wash and All was good until I saw the car in front of me hitting their brakes. My windshield was really soapy and I couldn't see what was going on but it seemed to me that I was getting  way too close to the car in front of me. I slammed on my brake at the last second because I saw through the soap on the windshield that I was about 4 inches away from the car in front of me. Had I not slammed my brakes and honked, the machine would have made me collide with the car in front of me. Only after I honked, I felt the machine power off. The workers only tended to the car in front of me. There was 2 long minutes of me sitting there watching the workers talk to the car in front of me and looking to check if we had collided. They NEVER CHECKED ON ME!!! I was so frightened by this incident, no one seemed to be paying attention to the cars, like I said, if I didn't have the insight to hit my brake, I would have slammed right into the car in front of me. I can't believe the workers never checked if I was okay. I payed $7 to prevent my car from a crash oh yeah, and a wash. Thankfully, no one was behind me or I'm sure I would have been rear ended. Beware in automatic car washes, they're not 100 percent safe, and then the workers won't even check if you're okay!!< /Review>

< Review>
This place is pretty good. It's clean, no roaches, the carpet and paint looked new. I was able to walk on the carpet barefooted and not feel grossed out. Towels are not soft, but they are clean. Not bad for the price and the owners are good. Internet is great. Sometimes it can be a little loud from the highway around 7:30 pm but it's quiet overnight. If you are in Downey for a week, stay in the motel and ask for the weekly rate. It's a better deal. Overall, this is a good place if you need to save money.< /Review>
